<rating>3<//rating><Text>When I first started going to Eureka Dental in 2010, I LOVED it! There was a dentist there that I absolutely trusted and did excellent work. Unfortunately, either this dentist left the practice or became completely unavailable because I've gone over a year since seeing him. Instead other dentists have been doing my work. They are competent and well meaning, however completely lack proper "bed-side manners" and attention to detail.
Each time I go in, they are short and don't ever bother to read my chart. They rarely ever explain recommended procedures, and then it's only after I insist on my questions being answered.
The issues that I do bring up, I feel, are brushed off. I have had problems with my lower gums and cavities on the bases of my teeth, I have been given different explanations each visit (even by the same doctor). It was the hygienists that actually gave me a reliable answer.
They are a little pricey. They also required me to pay everything upfront, before I even sat in the lobby. Normally not a problem, however sometimes this led me to being bulldozed by a $300+ bill because the treating dentist didn't bother to explain to me what was actually being done when I was given treatment options.
The reason my review is not lower is because of the office staff, they are AMAZING. Very friendly, helpful, and always willing to work with you. They gave me quotes after noticing that I was being blind sided with charges.
The only reason I haven't gone to a new dentist (until now) is because of the hygienists. They are awesome, kind and very gentle.
Overall, the dentists are very competent (even skilled), but since they have grown these little (but important) things that have gone by the wayside, making me take my teeth elsewhere.</Text>< pics>

<user>103479971306993223991</user><user_name>John R<//user_name><Date>1365267971888< /Date>< rating>

< text>
I recently acted on a promotion for a check up & cleaning through Eureka Dental. I could not be happier!  I was greeted at the door by two very professional and helpful ladies who directed me to a [really neat] computer station to enter my information.  I didn't even have time to get an idea of how comfortable the lobby furniture was because they got me in right away!

The Dental Hygienist (Mela) led me back to the chair while engaging in friendly small talk and giving me a quick tour of the office.  Her demeanor was very warm and upbeat, relaxing, and comfortable. The extra two minutes she took to let me adjust to the idea of allowing another person to introduce power tools in or near my mouth was much better than being marched back to the chair, sat down, and told to "open wide".  Her attention to detail was thorough and her technique of the hands-on part of the cleaning was impressive. I've seen RDH's with varying degrees of experience not nearly as good and gentle. As long as she is in the dental industry, she will be the only dental hygienist our family will see.

The dentist, Dr. Kaplan, examined my teeth with care and intense focus. He noticed almost all of my previous dental work via visual inspection. After examining the X-rays, he identified all of my previous dental work and pointed out a few potential problems. I was impressed because, although the technology EDG uses is very modern, it was obvious Dr. Kaplan is a great dentist even without all of the computer gadgets. The best way to describe it is "old school skills amplified by new innovative technology". I was given a concise break-down of the cost and importance of dental work I require.  I pay cash for my dental work, so this information was very helpful being organized by level of priority according to my health, NOT their bank account. I have savings contingencies allotted for different things including dental work.  When I explained that I needed a little time to save up for the work I need, they were not pushy nor have they blown up my email/phone trying to get me back in.

Most other offices I've visited have a very "clinical" vibe to them. Not at Eureka Dental! They provide complete dental care with comprehensive options. I will definitely be back and highly recommend Eureka Dental Group!</text>

<review>The laundry mat employees are typical two friendly ladies that will help you with any of the machines, if you need it. There is also a restroom located inside the building but you will need to have a quarter and an employee to let you in.

Washers and Dryers work great, and they have a variety of sizes for both uses. If you don't have or happen to forget soap/dryer sheets/fabric softener, don't worry, they have a vending machine inside that sells them all at your convenience. There is also a little mini arcade area with games kids can enjoy while waiting with their parents.

There is a good amount of seating and it wasn't that busy on a weekday night(4-6pm). Overall, great laundry mat.

P.S. A little tip, check the dryer machines for bent  metal that can possibly snag your clothes before putting your clothes in there. I only found one machine like that.</review>< response>

< Text>
I have had lots of good customer service here. I have yet to have a bad experience shopping here. One experience really sticks out. An employee named Mona helped me, and unlike the others she actually tried to create a conversation. I have worked customer service before, I know how hard it can be to keep a smile on my face and start conversations with random customers. Mona did a really good job at treating me almost as a friend instead of a customer. I hope that there are more cashiers like Mona that work in the future. <user_name>Rory Kagan</user_name><date>1606095808039<//date><rating>5<//rating><Text>I am a guy and notoriously have a difficult time with getting my hair cut.  I prefer it a bit lived in around the sides and to keep it at a medium-short length.  Whenever I go into a barbershop or salon, I request that they leave a little length around the ears, "the flips," and every time, I get the same short haircut.  Over the years, in a futile attempt to get the cut I had envisioned, I began changing what I request, bringing in pics and asking them to take less and less off each subsequent trip, and every time......same haircut.   The last haircut I got I walked in and said, "please don't cut it.".....walked out with the same haircut.
High and tight around the ears and short.  *Sigh...it'll grow in*
After having been scarred so many times, I obviously have reservations about getting my hair cut at all and rarely go.  Add in COVID and the mess on top of my head by November was worthy of the s%^* show that is the year we are all currently enduring.
My wife made the appointment for me because she needed a cut and color and couldn't look me in the face anymore, so we drove over an hour from Sebastopol down to SF.
On the way down, my wife asked me what kind of haircut I wanted and I cynically said, "what difference does it make...we know what I'm getting."
She coaxed me into pulling up some pics of hairstyles, and I found one of some model, who looks-wise I more resembled maybe the frog version of him before the princess kiss that magically transformed him into the guy who shows up on google searches for, "medium length hairstyles."  My wife and I agreed that the hair was at least close enough to be possible.  Did I mention that at 41 years of age I have this nice triangle of receding hair that lives right where I part my hair?  The long length combover to the side really couldn't do more to accentuate the sparsely populated patch on my head where the last few hair follicles are looking around saying, "where'd everybody go?"
The Salon itself is amazing.  My wife and I are very conservative when it comes to Covid and we haven't been out of our bubble much.  We worry a lot and let me say that with the precautions that CODE took, we didn't worry AT ALL.  Everyone was wearing masks the whole time and we were able to keep ours on for the entire appointments.
My appointment was with Denise and I sheepishly showed her the pic and requested she do what she can to help hide my balding spot.  To her credit, she didn't laugh at all as I had expected.  Quite the opposite.  She looked at the pic and actually really took it in.  She then spent time looking at my hair, moving it around, discussing the shape, length, all the while getting more enthusiastic about the cut.  "Let's do something fun!"  "Yea, we can do this."  ....like she was getting hyped up for the challenge.  I mention this because it was a unique experience for me.  She listened to what I said and really seemed motivated to actualize it.....to make some magic happen, akin to a sculptor looking at a block of lumpy clay and getting excited about the potential there.
Guess what.  For the first time in my life, I was awarded a new hairstyle!!!  She knocked it out of the park....made the impossible, possible.....and I am just thrilled.  My wife said I looked 20 years younger and my teen daughter, who typically reminds me that I have a receding hairline everyday, (lest I forget) was gushing over how good I looked.  My hair was such a freakin' mess that I was pretty self-conscious about it, opting to smash it down behind my ears and wear a hat all of the time.  I wasn't prepared for how much better I would feel walking out of there.  Denise is a true artist and from what my wife says, she is one of a whole team of them at CODE, which is why we were traveling an hour there to begin with.
I may not actually look like Google Search Hair Guy, but now I definitely feel like I do.....and I would be remiss not to mention that my wife also looks AMAZING!  Thank you, Denise, and thank you CODE!</Text><pictures>None</pictures>< Response>

Haircuts have been my least favorite thing to do for years because I always walk away super disappointed with the outcomes. < review>
This space started out like any other reclaimed building needed right away for events and art. What the Expo has done for Long Beach and Bixby Knolls has not only brought all outskirts to midtown but in my case got me out of my comfort zone. Allowing me to meet new people and find out more about my city. Atlantic Ave just past Wardlow is precious. The buildings , the little eateries , shops , the possibilities and the Expo. I've met many people at this creative space.   Watching a huge space evolve and grow I think is gratifying not only to those who participate but to anyone who comes to enjoy whatever is happening there at the time.< /review>

<text>I heard that Gogi Time was a good Korean BBQ place from a close friend, so I gave it a try and I was honestly so disappointed. The food and service were both lackluster and brought down the overall mood of my friend group. Here is why.

Lets start with the food. The food came in small portions (for a group of 5) and the quality of the meat was poor with fatty cuts. We had to cut out all the fat because it became too much in the end. We also ordered steamed egg as an appetizer and was absolutely disgusted when we scooped down to discover that the egg was barely cooked. When we showed this to our server, he merely brushed it off and said he would just add a new order of steamed egg to our next order. Our steamed egg failed to come and we had to ask again for the egg to come in at all. When the steamed egg did come in and was fully cooked, we tried it only to discover that it was too salty to even eat. We also ordered the soju cocktails and we could tell instantly that the soju wasn't the best quality because it was so hard to force down. Good soju is supposed to be smooth going down and have a crisp aftertaste but the cocktails here had a strange metallic taste to them. I believe in rating a restaurant based on the sole quality and taste of the food and this place gets a major disapproval from me.

Next is the service which doesn't affect my ratings but definitely impacts my experience and my mood towards this restaurant. Our server was barely present and rarely checked up on our table. We would eat and cook for 10 minutes and wait for 30 minutes just for the next set of meat to come in or to even get the server to take our order. When the server did get our order, he would constantly forget certain parts of our order and we would have to repeat it multiple times. Near the end we got fed up and just asked for the check because we were no longer in the mood to repeat ourselves or continue eating.

Overall Gogi Time fails to live up to the expectations that I have for Korean BBQ. For 30+ dollars and an additional 18% gratuity charge for any groups 5 or more, I feel that there are better options and the prices of the drinks here are overpriced considering the size and the quality of the drinks you receive.</text><Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipNDA3gOdRaGoxdJDQT9blCWZRX5CqqVEVANaizA=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipONA1YA9xBRGqmJIFikGcazdTZwX5hnWf7exYLM=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipOTA0xAAKLF3wIFLz6onoEUcCOI-GidhF-zE2PO=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPgI6pDr594hW8xOGrtVZEebID4mRHWB-5WSB5o=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]</Pics><Response>None<//Response>< gmap_id>

<pics>None< /pics>< Text>
Gogi Time has great food, hands down! It's all-you-can eat, which means you won't leave hungry, and there are many different items on the menu to choose from. It's a busy place any day of the week, especially starting around 5:30 pm. You will need to allow some time to find parking because the lot is tiny with a limited number of spaces. The area seemed safe and it's  generally clean.

The staff is quite friendly, but they are so busy that they forget orders quite often. There were several different food items I requested and had to repeat the request sometimes as many as three times. I didn't really mind because all the employees are so cheerful and positive. Their workload is high level for sure.

I spent about $83, which included the tip and one libation for my partner. I've dined at Gogi twice already, and I expect to go there again in the near future.< /Text>

<time>1583196550432<//time><Rating>4</Rating><Review>Sooo many options on the menu and it's great because it's all you can eat!
The meats were delicious and the variety of options for side dishes and soups were really great. It's been difficult to find a new korean bbq place I like in the bay area, but this is definitely one of my new favorites. The meat quality isn't amazing but it's great for the price you're paying.

The only con was that the service was slow, the order of meat we ordered never came so we sat with a hot grill for 10+ minutes before we realized they forgot about our order.

We also went a little early hoping to no have such a long wait time, we went at 6:30PM, they told us it would be a 30-40 minute wait, and it ended up being a 1.5hr wait instead.</Review><pics>None< /pics>< response>

<Review>If you're ever in the mood for some ALL YOU CAN EAT [NOT DRINK] kbbq with lots of friends or family this is the place. Gogi time is a Kbbq location where you order several kinds of meat and you grill it until ready.

They offer such a wide variety of options and since this is all you can eat I recommend their potstickers.

The hours I've gone late on a weekend after 9pm are typically packed and with long lines so if you want to be seated quickly I recommend going before 8pm.

Parking is pretty abysmal with maybe 15spots for gogi time but there is street parking across the street.

In a way it reminds me of Doctor Who's TARDIS, from Outside this place looks pretty small and unappealing but inside it's so lively and large that you forget about it. I recommend coming with atleast a party of 4 otherwise the wait can be even longer due to their seating arrangement for the grill.< /Review></record></dataset><record>

<text>It always starts with Wallace and him asking me "What's for lunch?"  Followed by "I don't know, what do you want?"  Then it always ends up being Korean or Sushi because he has to drive.  So the group is on the way for Korean food today, Pyeong Chang Tofu House, one of our regular places for Korean food.  We spot Gogi Time and said let's give it a try.  It was another Korean restaurant with a different name many years ago that I don't remember.  The place got a make over with new tables, new staff, new menu.  I got the Yuk Gae Jang which is spicy shredded beef soup.  My friend got the seafood tofu soup which he said was good, and our other friend got the spicy pork.  What I really like was that they provided lettuce to go with the spicy pork, most restaurants would charge for the lettuce, or it only comes when you get the BBQ (grill at the table).  The quantities are big here, and their Ban Chan (side dishes) came in larger plates than most people.   My bowl of soup was nice and spicy, it came with rice, but I couldn't eat much of it, it was just a lot of food.  What I like about this place is you can tell them who spicy you want your food.  I got medium, which was just right.

We were examining their all you can eat BBQ menu.  I was impressed that you could get appetizers as part of the BBQ meat. Most places you get the meat and the Ban Chan.  There was a table next to us that had ordered the BBQ and it looked good.  I think we're going to need to come back for the all you can eat BBQ for dinner.  They also have the hot pot in which you cook the meat in broth.< /text>< user_id>

< review>
We got there at 945pm a whole 45 min before their website says they close the kitchen. When we walked in we were told the kitchen was closed, and only alacart items were available, she then sat us down, put out the appetizers and a jug of water and forced us to order right there. She then disappeared for the entirety of our time there and didnt hand off our table to anyone else. She forgot cups, chopsticks, bowls, napkins and plates. We didnt get the latter until we flagged down 2 different servers to get the items we needed to eat the soup. We also had to wonder around the resturant to get the napkins, chopsticks and cups. Finally the food was probably the worst Korean food I've ever had. The bul gogi was essentially some meat with VERY light sauce, like so light it was hardly distinguishable from just meat. The soup my wife ordered had the most subpar meat that I've ever had. I began to question whether this meat was meant for human consumption, but the broth was pretty good. Finally some of the workers got off and were just a loud nusance the whole time we were eating. They were just standing in a circle by the door shouting at each other. Worst part is we live soo close but will obviously never come here again. Id rather sit in 2 hours of traffic to get to sj for some good Korean BBQ than sit through that again.</review>

<username>Eric Tam</username><Date>1533063012456< /Date>< Rate>

< text>
Not the cheapest, just the best! The wait here can be unbearable but if you have a large party you can call ahead for a reservation. Although it's not written anywhere, the AYCE is two hours.  Year ago they use to use charcoal (which in my opinion) was more flavorful. Instead they switch to gas grills.

There's many pluses here starting with the large tables. Unlike some other AYCE that can only fit a dish or two, you can actually load up four or five dishes with room to spare. Their side dishes aren't the star here and their appetizers comes in nice small portions. A tofu soup is the size of two rice bowl and their Kimchi Pancake has nine small pieces.

Their sodas come in a can, but for a meal like this, try their Soji Sake bomb. It's not something to get drunk of but very refreshing with the BBQ meal.< /text>

<UserId.>102338226077530057723</UserId.><Name>Art Del Mundo<//Name><date>1485713019147<//date><rate>5< /rate><review>First time eating here.  Came for a friend's going away party.  Right near the West Grand/27th exit in Oakland.  First off, parking can be hard here as the restaurant shares a parking lot with a billiards and another bar/restaurant.  At night, you can park on the street during times when the parking meters are not enforced.  During my visit there, I only had the KBBQ and not the hot pot.  Grills were really nice.  They use cast iron grills so meats tend to not stick on the grills while cooking and don't need to be changed quite as often.  That is a plus in my opinion.  Ordered the spicy pork, bulgogi, thin sliced brisket, short rib tips, corn, zucchini,  rice cake and tofu soup.  Marinade on the meats tasted good and the slices were thick but thin enough to cook quick.  Good selection of banchan to eat while food was cooking on the grills.  The only criticism I have is the selection is not as extensive as Gen Korean BBQ which is roughly the same price for dinner.  Overall, the experience was good, service was speedy and attentive and the food was good (as long as the person cooking does it right!).</review><pictures>None</pictures>< Resp>

<Gmap_id>0x808f80ab0f1348a9:0x4923b85dffacff92<//Gmap_id><Text>$25/pp... for all you can eat hotpot or all you can eat BBQ. We did the hotpot and it included meats, ramens, dumplings, kimchi pancakes (they don't go into the hotpot), veggies... basically an extraordinarily extensive menu. All for $25. My San Francisco mind was blown and I kept looking for the fine print. Okay, they'll charge you if you don't finish the meat, but basically just don't be pathetic and finish your food. Also don't be a turd and order everything off the menu... unless you've had an especially grueling workout that day.

I'm used to going to Little Sheep Hotpot in SF, paying a la carte, and getting a bill of approximately $60-70/pp so I spent the meal beaming at my husband happily over the fact that I could order anything I wanted off the menu with impunity.

There are 6 main broths to choose from (we got half and half Mongolian spice and tom yom spice... which both tasted pretty unidentifiable from each other but were nice and spicy). I am a spice fiend, so I might ask for one to be extra spicy next time (both the soup and my face need to be bright fluorescent red before I'm fully happy).

Service was a bit scattered (it gets BUSY) but I absolutely enjoyed the meal. Pork and corn dumplings and the ribeye were particularly good.
Can't wait to go back. Next time... BBQ!<//Text>< Date>

<Rate>4</Rate>< Text>
VERY popular korean barbecue place in Oakland. There is a parking lot (both front and back) and plenty of street parking. Come either early or late, before 6pm or after 9pm, if you don't want to wait an hour or more for a table. They got rid of the charcoal grilling, FYI.

AYCE is about $25 and comes with different kinds of meat (includes pretty decent kalbi), seafood, veggies, and various appetizers (like corn cheese, pancake, soondobu, japchae, potstickers). Service can be pretty shotty, which is my only complaint. There is a 2 hour limit, but you shouldn't need that long as the meat portions are pretty healthy, and they allow you to order up to 5 things at once. Get an order of the ssam platter for the garlic and soybean paste.

Banchan is pretty decent, but you have to ask to get refilled. Pro tip: the kimchi is muchly improved if you grill it.

As for meats, the kalbi, spicy marinated pork, pork belly, and perhaps bulgolgi is all you should really care to eat. The rest are just filler and mediocre.</Text>

<UserId.>105818373356803739204< /UserId.><username>Jiann Mok<//username>< date>
1426272526121</date>
<Rate>4< /Rate>< Review>
Tips:
- wear clothes you don't care about. You WILL smell like BBQ afterward
- note that they use charcoal grills, not gas

Pros:
- pretty good beef (bulgogi and spicy bulgogi were my favs)
- charcoal grills make the beef taste more BBQ-y than a gas stove
- good for large events (our 40+ people were seated in the back room)
- friendly staff who brought out all the dipping sauces and side dishes before we even thought to ask

Cons:
- grill stands above table, making it difficult to cook while seated
- charcoal is super hot and might make you tear up several times throughout the meal
- kimchi pancake is alright, but not like traditional Korean pancakes (it'll taste better if you grill it)
- $25 for all-you-can-eat KBBQ (compare to LA's average price of $20, before tax and tip)
- exhaust vents are practically useless
- you will smell like smoke and BBQ afterward (but that comes with any KBBQ)

Bottom line: This is one of the better KBBQ in East Bay. I still like LA KBBQ better (which is also cheaper), but I would probably come here again.</Review>

<time>1392865117458< /time><rating>3</rating><review>PSA: REALLY SMOKY INSIDE.

Came with a group of 6 to do the AYCE hot pot and bbq. We ordered the kimchi pancake to start, eh it was ok. Nothing special.

For the BBQ I was bummed there was no baby octopus. Or mussels. So the only thing I ate from the BBQ was chicken and squid. The rest of my party ordered tons of meats. For the hot pot we ordered a ton too!

Besides being completely out of a few of the menu items, the food was pretty good. I liked how they cook it on a charcoal rather than flame, so that can account for all the smoke in the restaurant...but still, SO SMOKY (I've never used this word so much in my life...)

However, the service was horrible. I understand it's a new restaurant (hence, the potential for being 4 stars...) but as of now, I'll keep it at 3. I guess being in the back room was a disadvantage because servers would forget we were back there. To the point where they'd come in looking at their cell phone, and then look up and be surprised people where eating.

There were multiple servers going in and out to try and place our orders, sometimes we'd get it quickly and other times servers would bring multiple things back. It was just slow. And when splitting the checks, it took a bit since the system (and servers) are all new. Then, they split the check's wrong. But it took long enough to get it so we just paid it.

But everyone was nice and friendly, so that's always a plus.
